<div id="review_604852697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604852697" />
    <a title="Bandit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit"><img alt="Bandit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289488158p2/4528663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604852697?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bandit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bandit" href="/user/show/4528663-bandit">Bandit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780739312124" href="/book/show/1776879.The_Taking">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604852697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15880011348915531046">Leave it up to the literary equivalent of Wonderbread that Koontz is to mess up even something as fun an an alien invasion story. Actually I don't know if comparing him to Wonderbread might not be misleading due the word wonder in the brand name, something that is always in deficit in Koontz' work. But to pick up Koontz' book with all the great books that are out there would be like passing by a freshly baked baguette for a loaf of Wonderbread and for the sake of this analogy let's assume the pr</span>
  <span id="freeText15880011348915531046" style="display:none">Leave it up to the literary equivalent of Wonderbread that Koontz is to mess up even something as fun an an alien invasion story. Actually I don't know if comparing him to Wonderbread might not be misleading due the word wonder in the brand name, something that is always in deficit in Koontz' work. But to pick up Koontz' book with all the great books that are out there would be like passing by a freshly baked baguette for a loaf of Wonderbread and for the sake of this analogy let's assume the price of no importance. So, this was an audio book I picked up forever ago and slowly walked and biked my way through over the course of many months. I figured I should get something ok, but not great so that it could provide a background entertainment, but it wouldn't matter if a blasting car horn or something bleeped out some of the lines. This book didn't even meet those low criteria levels. Koontz, never shy about pushing, shoving and cramming his limited world views upon his readers, has turned what should have been a fun alien story into basically a lecture about his religious views and capital punishment/judicial system opinions. And with his trademarks of cast of cardboard cutouts, complete lack of character development and pervasive and unnecessary oversimplifications and repetitions, this book really has nothing to offer in a way of quality or interest. He did read enough of T.S. Eliot to quote all throughout the book achieving the literary equivalent of throwing diamonds among the dirt. Can't imagine why, other than he probably doesn't see it that way. He might actually think Eliot's writing would be complimentary to his. There's obviously some delusion at work here, particularly considering how well Koontz sells. But then again, so does Wonderbread...now quite appropriately distributed by Bimbo corporation. So yeah, stupid book, don't bother, not worth the time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15880011348915531046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24851326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24851326" />
    <a title="Kevin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/674412-kevin"><img alt="Kevin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545617938p2/674412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24851326?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin" href="/user/show/674412-kevin">Kevin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24851326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3559319314137234306">After being awoken by an uncharacteristically powerful, oddly fragrant, and eerily luminescent rainfall, Molly and Neil Sloan discover that some kind of alien takeover of the Earth is in progress. Scared beyond wit's end but knowing that they are not going to give up without a fight, the couple pack up supplies and venture out into the darkness to discover if any of their neighbors are still alive and who would be willing to take up arms against an enemy who has yet to show himself. As time trud</span>
  <span id="freeText3559319314137234306" style="display:none">After being awoken by an uncharacteristically powerful, oddly fragrant, and eerily luminescent rainfall, Molly and Neil Sloan discover that some kind of alien takeover of the Earth is in progress. Scared beyond wit's end but knowing that they are not going to give up without a fight, the couple pack up supplies and venture out into the darkness to discover if any of their neighbors are still alive and who would be willing to take up arms against an enemy who has yet to show himself. As time trudges slowly on and Molly and Neil uncover the atrocities perpetrated by this alien species, they find their priorities changing as they begin a new fight for survival. As soon as you open the book, Koontz grabs a hold of you and pulls you in to this world. Taking elements of all the great science fiction classics, but giving them a Koontz twist, you just can't help but want to read more. The author's descriptiveness and eloquence is second to none and very different considering the genre in which he is writing, but it really helps place you in the moment and allows you to view the action exactly as he does. My only problem is just how abruptly it ends. I think it could have been carried out even further than it was. And I wish it was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3559319314137234306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_470009143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/470009143" />

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/470009143?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/9857088-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007130771" href="/book/show/959357.The_Taking">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9857088-liz?shelf=have-book">have-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9857088-liz?shelf=that-s-sum-scary-shit">that-s-sum-scary-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer470009143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18260500891498504148">This was a surprisingly good read for what I thought would be a pulp fiction horror. Koonzt is actually a really talented author, his descriptions are like the Thomas Hardy of horror....ok maybe not as talented, but close.<br/><br/>Zoontz builds an atmosphere in the first two pages and he continues to build tension and suspense through his descriptions of the surroundings and his characters. If it had rained whilst I read this book, I probably would have felt a little freaked out myself.<br/><br/>My only complaint </span>
  <span id="freeText18260500891498504148" style="display:none">This was a surprisingly good read for what I thought would be a pulp fiction horror. Koonzt is actually a really talented author, his descriptions are like the Thomas Hardy of horror....ok maybe not as talented, but close.<br /><br />Zoontz builds an atmosphere in the first two pages and he continues to build tension and suspense through his descriptions of the surroundings and his characters. If it had rained whilst I read this book, I probably would have felt a little freaked out myself.<br /><br />My only complaint is that the ending feels really really rushed. It was like he presented his publisher with a 700 page manuscript and his publisher was like 'ah, the types of people that read your horror books only like 450 pages max' There was so much texture and substance to this story that moved at the right pace and then all of a sudden in one chapter the climax occurs and then the last 10-20 pages tie loose ends. The ending did not do the story justice!<br /><br />From now on I'm going to put Stephen King horror novels on the back burner and get into some Koontz </span>
  <a data-text-id="18260500891498504148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ehvB2tcxFS4CjAMCk+E7CF6XwK9b0j6EabVyPO1HjMJucRkgwzM5gB2Jy8ZdDrQP4bb35sg/VRXHuP+bAdZc8w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YQsX6dbGCiCBxVqgBFRE7zRP1hACabzO1n6PtJ650Gl1Yc8TwsQmjp7AkmTKu8voi27hWZGE1194cwITcigAWA==')})
  }
//]]>
